     <p>
      <b>
       Tobacco smoking
      </b>
      is the practice of burning
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">
       tobacco
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">
       inhaling the smoke
      </a>
      (consisting of particle and gaseous phases). (A more broad definition may include simply taking tobacco smoke into the mouth, and then releasing it, as is done by some with tobacco pipes and cigars.) The practice was believed to begin as early as 50003000 BC .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gateley2004_1-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gateley2004-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tobacco was introduced to
      <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">
       Eurasia
      </a>
      in the late 17th century where it followed common trade routes. The practice encountered criticism from its first import into the Western world onwards, but embedded itself in certain strata of a number of societies before becoming widespread upon the introduction of automated
      <a href="/wiki/Cigarette" title="Cigarette">
       cigarette
      </a>
      -rolling apparatus.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L.26M_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-L.26M-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      German scientists identified a link between smoking and lung cancer in the late 1920s, leading to the first
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-smoking_campaign" title="Anti-smoking campaign">
       anti-smoking campaign
      </a>
      in modern history, albeit one truncated by the collapse of the Third Reich at the end of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">
       Second World War
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC228_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC228-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1950, British researchers demonstrated a clear relationship between smoking and cancer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RichardHillyBMJ1954_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RichardHillyBMJ1954-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Evidence continued to mount in the 1980s, which prompted political action against the practice. Rates of consumption since 1965 in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_world" title="Developed world">
       developed world
      </a>
      have either peaked or declined.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RockEtAlCDC2006_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RockEtAlCDC2006-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, they continue to climb in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">
       developing world
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2002FactSheet_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2002FactSheet-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Smoking is the most common method of consuming tobacco, and tobacco is the most common substance smoked. The agricultural product is often mixed with additives
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOJeffreyWigand_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHOJeffreyWigand-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and then
      <a href="/wiki/Combustion" title="Combustion">
       combusted
      </a>
      . The resulting smoke is then inhaled and the active substances absorbed through the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveoli" title="Alveoli">
       alveoli
      </a>
      in the lungs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GilmanXun2004p318_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GilmanXun2004p318-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Combustion was traditionally enhanced by addition of potassium or other nitrates.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Many substances in cigarette smoke trigger chemical reactions in nerve endings, which heighten heart rate, alertness,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PMID2498936_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-PMID2498936-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and reaction time, among other things.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WesnessWarburton1997_11-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WesnessWarburton1997-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Dopamine" title="Dopamine">
       Dopamine
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endorphin" title="Endorphin">
       endorphins
      </a>
      are released, which are often associated with pleasure.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GilmanXun2004pp320-321_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GilmanXun2004pp320-321-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2008 to 2010, tobacco is used by about 3billion people (about 49% of men and 11% of women) with about 80% of this usage in the form of smoking.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The gender gap tends to be less pronounced in lower age groups.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WomenTobaccoChallenges5-6_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WomenTobaccoChallenges5-6-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001SurgeonGeneralWomen47_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-2001SurgeonGeneralWomen47-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Many smokers begin during
      <a href="/wiki/Adolescence" title="Adolescence">
       adolescence
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_adulthood" title="Early adulthood">
       early adulthood
      </a>
      . During the early stages, a combination of perceived pleasure acting as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_reinforcement" title="Positive reinforcement">
       positive reinforcement
      </a>
      and desire to respond to social peer pressure may offset the unpleasant symptoms of initial use, which typically include nausea and coughing. After an individual has smoked for some years, the avoidance of
      <a href="/wiki/Drug_withdrawal" title="Drug withdrawal">
       withdrawal
      </a>
      symptoms and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Negative_reinforcement" title="Negative reinforcement">
       negative reinforcement
      </a>
      become the key motivations to continue.
     </p>
     <p>
      In a study done by Jennifer O' Loughlin and her colleagues, the first smoking experiences of seventh-grade students were studied.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Lancet_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Lancet-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They found out that the most common factor leading students to smoke is cigarette advertisements. Smoking by parents, siblings and friends also encourage students to smoke.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Lancet_16-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-The_Lancet-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_tobacco" title="History of tobacco">
       History of tobacco
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_smoking" title="History of smoking">
       History of smoking
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Use_in_ancient_cultures">
       Use in ancient cultures
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Use in ancient cultures">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aztec_feast_1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="966" data-file-width="910" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Aztec_feast_1.jpg/220px-Aztec_feast_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Aztec_feast_1.jpg/330px-Aztec_feast_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Aztec_feast_1.jpg/440px-Aztec_feast_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aztec_feast_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Aztec women are handed flowers and smoking tubes before eating at a banquet,
        <a href="/wiki/Florentine_Codex" title="Florentine Codex">
         Florentine Codex
        </a>
        , 16th century.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Smoking's history dates back to as early as 50003000 BC when the agricultural product began to be cultivated in South America; consumption later evolved into burning the plant substance either by accident or with intent of exploring other means of consumption.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gateley2004_1-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Gateley2004-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The practice worked its way into shamanistic rituals.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilbert1993_17-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Wilbert1993-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many ancient civilisations  such as the Babylonians, the Indians, and the Chinese  burnt incense during religious rituals. The practice was later adopted by Christians. Smoking in the Americas probably had its origins in the incense-burning ceremonies of
      <a href="/wiki/Shamanism" title="Shamanism">
       shamans
      </a>
      but was later adopted for pleasure or as a social tool.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Robicsek1979_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Robicsek1979-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The smoking of tobacco and various hallucinogenic drugs was used to achieve trances and to come into contact with the spirit world.
     </p>
     <p>
      Eastern North American tribes would carry large amounts of tobacco in pouches as a readily accepted trade item and would often smoke it in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peace_pipe" title="Peace pipe">
       pipes
      </a>
      , either in sacred ceremonies or to seal bargains.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Adults as well as children enjoyed the practice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was believed that tobacco was a gift from the Creator and that the exhaled tobacco smoke was capable of carrying one's thoughts and prayers to heaven.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Apart from smoking, tobacco had a number of uses as medicine. As a pain killer it was used for earache and toothache and occasionally as a
      <a href="/wiki/Poultice" title="Poultice">
       poultice
      </a>
      . Smoking was said by the desert Indians to be a cure for colds, especially if the tobacco was mixed with the leaves of the small Desert Sage,
      <i>
       Salvia Dorrii
      </i>
      , or the root of Indian Balsam or Cough Root,
      <i>
       Leptotaenia multifida
      </i>
      , the addition of which was thought to be particularly good for asthma and tuberculosis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Popularization">
       Popularization
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Popularization">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      For more about the commercial development of tobacco, see
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_commercial_tobacco_in_the_United_States" title="History of commercial tobacco in the United States">
       History of commercial tobacco in the United States
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="409" data-file-width="550" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg/230px-Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg/345px-Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg/460px-Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg 2x" width="230"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gentlemen_Smoking_and_Playing_Backgammon_in_an_Interior.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <i>
         Gentlemen Smoking and Playing Backgammon in an Interior
        </i>
        by
        <a href="/wiki/Dirck_Hals" title="Dirck Hals">
         Dirck Hals
        </a>
        , 1627.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1612, six years after the settlement of Jamestown,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Rolfe" title="John Rolfe">
       John Rolfe
      </a>
      was credited as the first settler to successfully raise tobacco as a cash crop. The demand quickly grew as tobacco, referred to as "brown gold", revived the Virginia joint stock company from its failed gold expeditions.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In order to meet demands from the Old World, tobacco was grown in succession, quickly depleting the soil. This became a motivator to settle west into the unknown continent, and likewise an expansion of tobacco production.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indentured_servitude" title="Indentured servitude">
       Indentured servitude
      </a>
      became the primary labor force up until
      <a href="/wiki/Bacon%27s_Rebellion" title="Bacon's Rebellion">
       Bacon's Rebellion
      </a>
      , from which the focus turned to slavery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This trend abated following the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_revolution" title="American revolution">
       American revolution
      </a>
      as slavery became regarded as unprofitable. However, the practice was revived in 1794 with the invention of the cotton gin.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Frenchman
      <a href="/wiki/Jean_Nicot" title="Jean Nicot">
       Jean Nicot
      </a>
      (from whose name the word nicotine is derived) introduced tobacco to France in 1560, and tobacco then spread to England. The first report of a smoking Englishman is of a sailor in Bristol in 1556, seen "emitting smoke from his nostrils".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L.26M_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-L.26M-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Like tea, coffee and opium, tobacco was just one of many intoxicants that was originally used as a form of medicine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tobacco was introduced around 1600 by French merchants in what today is modern-day
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gambia" title="Gambia">
       Gambia
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">
       Senegal
      </a>
      . At the same time caravans from
      <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      brought tobacco to the areas around
      <a href="/wiki/Timbuktu" title="Timbuktu">
       Timbuktu
      </a>
      and the Portuguese brought the commodity (and the plant) to southern Africa, establishing the popularity of tobacco throughout all of Africa by the 1650s.
     </p>
     <p>
      Soon after its introduction to the Old World, tobacco came under frequent criticism from state and religious leaders.
      <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">
       James VI and I
      </a>
      , King of Scotland and England, produced the treatise
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Counterblaste_to_Tobacco" title="A Counterblaste to Tobacco">
        A Counterblaste to Tobacco
       </a>
      </i>
      in 1604, and also introduced excise duty on the product.
      <a href="/wiki/Murad_IV" title="Murad IV">
       Murad IV
      </a>
      , sultan of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
       Ottoman Empire
      </a>
      1623-40 was among the first to attempt a smoking ban by claiming it was a threat to public morals and health. The Chinese emperor
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chongzhen" title="Chongzhen">
       Chongzhen
      </a>
      issued an edict banning smoking two years before his death and the overthrow of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ming_dynasty" title="Ming dynasty">
       Ming dynasty
      </a>
      . Later, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manchu" title="Manchu">
       Manchu
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Qing_dynasty" title="Qing dynasty">
       Qing dynasty
      </a>
      , would proclaim smoking "a more heinous crime than that even of neglecting archery". In
      <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">
       Edo period
      </a>
      Japan, some of the earliest tobacco plantations were scorned by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shogunate" title="Shogunate">
       shogunate
      </a>
      as being a threat to the military economy by letting valuable farmland go to waste for the use of a recreational drug instead of being used to plant food crops.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Screech-Smoke_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Screech-Smoke-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bonsack_machine.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1584" data-file-width="1897" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bonsack_machine.png/220px-Bonsack_machine.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bonsack_machine.png/330px-Bonsack_machine.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bonsack_machine.png/440px-Bonsack_machine.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bonsack_machine.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Bonsack's cigarette rolling machine, as shown on U.S. patent 238,640.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Religious leaders have often been prominent among those who considered smoking immoral or outright blasphemous. In 1634 the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriarch_of_Moscow" title="Patriarch of Moscow">
       Patriarch of Moscow
      </a>
      forbade the sale of tobacco, and sentenced men and women who flouted the ban to have their nostrils slit and their backs flayed. The Western church leader
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_VII" title="Urban VII">
       Urban VII
      </a>
      likewise condemned smoking on holy places in a papal bull of 1624. Despite some concerted efforts, restrictions and bans were largely ignored. When
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_I_of_England" title="James I of England">
       James I of England
      </a>
      , a staunch anti-smoker and the author of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A_Counterblaste_to_Tobacco" title="A Counterblaste to Tobacco">
        A Counterblaste to Tobacco
       </a>
      </i>
      , tried to curb the new trend by enforcing a 4000% tax increase on tobacco in 1604 it was unsuccessful, as suggested by the presence of around 7,000 tobacco outlets in London by the early 17th century. From this point on for some centuries, several administrations withdrew from efforts at discouragement and instead turned tobacco trade and cultivation into sometimes lucrative government monopolies.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      By the mid-17th century most major civilisations had been introduced to tobacco smoking and in many cases had already assimilated it into the native culture, despite some continued attempts upon the parts of rulers to eliminate the practice with penalties or fines. Tobacco, both product and plant, followed the major trade routes to major ports and markets, and then on into the hinterlands. The English language term
      <i>
       smoking
      </i>
      appears to have entered currency in the late 18th century, before which less abbreviated descriptions of the practice such as
      <i>
       drinking smoke
      </i>
      were also in use.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-L.26M_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-L.26M-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Growth in the US remained stable until the American Civil War in 1860s, when the primary agricultural workforce shifted from
      <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
       slavery
      </a>
      to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Share_cropping" title="Share cropping">
       share cropping
      </a>
      . This, along with a change in demand, accompanied the industrialisation of cigarette production as craftsman
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Bonsack" title="James Bonsack">
       James Bonsack
      </a>
      created a machine in 1881 to partially automate their manufacture.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burns134-135_31-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Burns134-135-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_attitudes_and_public_health">
       Social attitudes and public health
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Social attitudes and public health">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lewis_Hine,_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch,_St._Louis,_1910.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4043" data-file-width="5000" height="178" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Lewis_Hine%2C_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch%2C_St._Louis%2C_1910.jpg/220px-Lewis_Hine%2C_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch%2C_St._Louis%2C_1910.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Lewis_Hine%2C_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch%2C_St._Louis%2C_1910.jpg/330px-Lewis_Hine%2C_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch%2C_St._Louis%2C_1910.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Lewis_Hine%2C_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch%2C_St._Louis%2C_1910.jpg/440px-Lewis_Hine%2C_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch%2C_St._Louis%2C_1910.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lewis_Hine,_Newsies_smoking_at_Skeeter%27s_Branch,_St._Louis,_1910.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Newsies smoking at Skeeter's Branch, St. Louis, MO. Photograph by Lewis Hine, 1910
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In Germany, anti-smoking groups, often associated with anti-liquor groups,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC178_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC178-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      first published advocacy against the consumption of tobacco in the journal
      <i>
       Der Tabakgegner
      </i>
      (The Tobacco Opponent) in 1912 and 1932. In 1929,
      <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Lickint" title="Fritz Lickint">
       Fritz Lickint
      </a>
      of Dresden, Germany, published a paper containing formal statistical evidence of a lung cancertobacco link. During the Great Depression
      <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
       Adolf Hitler
      </a>
      condemned his earlier smoking habit as a waste of money,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC219_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC219-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and later with stronger assertions. This movement was further strengthened with Nazi reproductive policy as women who smoked were viewed as unsuitable to be wives and mothers in a German family.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC187_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC187-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Anti-tobacco_movement_in_Nazi_Germany" title="Anti-tobacco movement in Nazi Germany">
       anti-tobacco movement in Nazi Germany
      </a>
      did not reach across enemy lines during the Second World War, as anti-smoking groups quickly lost popular support. By the end of the Second World War, American cigarette manufacturers quickly reentered the German black market. Illegal smuggling of tobacco became prevalent,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC245_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC245-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and leaders of the Nazi anti-smoking campaign were silenced.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADLNMPHP_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-ADLNMPHP-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">
       Marshall Plan
      </a>
      , the United States shipped free tobacco to Germany; with 24,000 tons in 1948 and 69,000tons in 1949.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC245_35-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC245-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Per capita yearly cigarette consumption in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Germany_since_1945" title="History of Germany since 1945">
       post-war Germany
      </a>
      steadily rose from 460 in 1950 to 1,523 in 1963.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC228_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC228-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By the end of the 20th century, anti-smoking campaigns in Germany were unable to exceed the effectiveness of the Nazi-era climax in the years 193941 and German tobacco health research was described by
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_N._Proctor" title="Robert N. Proctor">
       Robert N. Proctor
      </a>
      as "muted".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NWC228_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-NWC228-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="318" data-file-width="326" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg/220px-Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg/330px-Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg/440px-Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cancer_smoking_lung_cancer_correlation_from_NIH.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A lengthy study conducted in order to establish the strong association necessary for legislative action
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1950,
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Doll" title="Richard Doll">
       Richard Doll
      </a>
      published research in the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Medical_Journal" title="British Medical Journal">
        British Medical Journal
       </a>
      </i>
      showing a close link between smoking and
      <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">
       lung cancer
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Beginning in December 1952, the magazine
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Reader%27s_Digest" title="Reader's Digest">
        Reader's Digest
       </a>
      </i>
      published "Cancer by the Carton", a series of articles that linked
      <a href="/wiki/Smoking" title="Smoking">
       smoking
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">
       lung cancer
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1954, the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Doctors_Study" title="British Doctors Study">
       British Doctors Study
      </a>
      , a study of some 40 thousand doctors over 20 years, confirmed the suggestion, based on which the government issued advice that smoking and lung cancer rates were related.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RichardHillyBMJ1954_5-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-RichardHillyBMJ1954-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In January 1964, the United States
      <a href="/wiki/Surgeon_General_of_the_United_States" title="Surgeon General of the United States">
       Surgeon General
      </a>
      's Report on Smoking and Health likewise began suggesting the relationship between smoking and cancer.
     </p>
     <p>
      As scientific evidence mounted in the 1980s, tobacco companies claimed
      <a href="/wiki/Contributory_negligence" title="Contributory negligence">
       contributory negligence
      </a>
      as the adverse health effects were previously unknown or lacked substantial credibility. Health authorities sided with these claims up until 1998, from which they reversed their position. The
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_Master_Settlement_Agreement" title="Tobacco Master Settlement Agreement">
       Tobacco Master Settlement Agreement
      </a>
      , originally between the four largest US tobacco companies and the Attorneys General of 46 states, restricted certain types of tobacco advertisement and required payments for health compensation; which later amounted to the largest civil settlement in United States history.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WallStreetJournalTobaccoMastersSettlement_39-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WallStreetJournalTobaccoMastersSettlement-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Social campaigns have been instituted in many places to discourage smoking, such as Canada's
      <a href="/wiki/National_Non-Smoking_Week" title="National Non-Smoking Week">
       National Non-Smoking Week
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      From 1965 to 2006, rates of smoking in the United States declined from 42% to 20.8%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RockEtAlCDC2006_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-RockEtAlCDC2006-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The majority of those who quit were professional, affluent men. Although the per-capita number of smokers decreased, the average number of cigarettes consumed per person per day increased from 22 in 1954 to 30 in 1978. This paradoxical event suggests that those who quit smoked less, while those who continued to smoke moved to smoke more light cigarettes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The trend has been paralleled by many industrialized nations as rates have either leveled-off or declined. In the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">
       developing world
      </a>
      , however, tobacco consumption continues to rise at 3.4% in 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2002FactSheet_7-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2002FactSheet-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In Africa, smoking is in most areas considered to be modern, and many of the strong adverse opinions that prevail in the West receive much less attention.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Today Russia leads as the top consumer of tobacco followed by
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">
       Laos
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
       Ukraine
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">
       Belarus
      </a>
      , Greece,
      <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">
       Jordan
      </a>
      , and China.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPOWER_2008_pp.3D267.E2.80.93288_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-MPOWER_2008_pp.3D267.E2.80.93288-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Consumption">
       Consumption
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Consumption">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Methods">
       Methods
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Methods">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      For more about the production of the agricultural product, see
      <a href="/wiki/Cultivation_of_tobacco" title="Cultivation of tobacco">
       Cultivation of tobacco
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Types_of_tobacco" title="Types of tobacco">
       Types of tobacco
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Curing_of_tobacco" title="Curing of tobacco">
       Curing of tobacco
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_products" title="Tobacco products">
       Tobacco products
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">
       Tobacco
      </a>
      is an agricultural product processed from the fresh leaves of plants in the genus
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nicotiana" title="Nicotiana">
        Nicotiana
       </a>
      </i>
      . The genus contains a number of species, however,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nicotiana_tabacum" title="Nicotiana tabacum">
        Nicotiana tabacum
       </a>
      </i>
      is the most commonly grown.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nicotiana_rustica" title="Nicotiana rustica">
        Nicotiana rustica
       </a>
      </i>
      follows as second containing higher concentrations of nicotine. These leaves are harvested and cured to allow for the slow
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxidation" title="Oxidation">
       oxidation
      </a>
      and degradation of
      <a href="/wiki/Carotenoid" title="Carotenoid">
       carotenoids
      </a>
      in tobacco leaf. This produces certain compounds in the tobacco leaves which can be attributed to sweet hay, tea, rose oil, or fruity aromatic flavors. Before packaging, the tobacco is often combined with other additives in order to enhance the addictive potency, shift the products
      <a href="/wiki/PH" title="PH">
       pH
      </a>
      , or improve the effects of smoke by making it more palatable. In the United States these additives are regulated to
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_additives_in_cigarettes" title="List of additives in cigarettes">
       599 substances
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOJeffreyWigand_8-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHOJeffreyWigand-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The product is then processed, packaged, and shipped to consumer markets.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:184px;max-width:184px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nicotiana_Tobacco_Plants_1909px.jpg">
          <img alt="Field of tobacco organized in rows extending to the horizon." data-file-height="2953" data-file-width="1840" height="289" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Nicotiana_Tobacco_Plants_1909px.jpg/180px-Nicotiana_Tobacco_Plants_1909px.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Nicotiana_Tobacco_Plants_1909px.jpg/270px-Nicotiana_Tobacco_Plants_1909px.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Nicotiana_Tobacco_Plants_1909px.jpg/360px-Nicotiana_Tobacco_Plants_1909px.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Tobacco field in
         <a href="/wiki/Intercourse,_Pennsylvania" title="Intercourse, Pennsylvania">
          Intercourse, Pennsylvania
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Basma-tobacco-drying.jpg">
          <img alt="Powderly stripps hung vertically, slightly sun bleached." data-file-height="3366" data-file-width="4768" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Basma-tobacco-drying.jpg/180px-Basma-tobacco-drying.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Basma-tobacco-drying.jpg/270px-Basma-tobacco-drying.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Basma-tobacco-drying.jpg/360px-Basma-tobacco-drying.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tobacco_leaves" title="Tobacco leaves">
          Basma
         </a>
         leaves curing in the sun at
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pomak" title="Pomak">
          Pomak
         </a>
         village of
         <a href="/wiki/Xanthi" title="Xanthi">
          Xanthi
         </a>
         , Thrace, Greece.
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DunhillLightFlake.jpg">
          <img alt="Rectangular strips stacked in an open square box." data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/DunhillLightFlake.jpg/180px-DunhillLightFlake.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/DunhillLightFlake.jpg/270px-DunhillLightFlake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/DunhillLightFlake.jpg/360px-DunhillLightFlake.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Processed tobacco pressed into flakes for pipe smoking.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Beedi
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <a href="/wiki/Beedi" title="Beedi">
        Beedis
       </a>
       are thin South Asian cigarettes filled with tobacco flakes and wrapped in a tendu leaf tied with a string at one end. They produce higher levels of carbon monoxide, nicotine, and tar than cigarettes typical in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         43
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         44
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Diospyros_melanoxylon_Tendu.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="402" height="274" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Diospyros_melanoxylon_Tendu.jpg/220px-Diospyros_melanoxylon_Tendu.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Diospyros_melanoxylon_Tendu.jpg/330px-Diospyros_melanoxylon_Tendu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/Diospyros_melanoxylon_Tendu.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Diospyros_melanoxylon_Tendu.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Tendu Patta (Leaf) Collection for Beedi industries
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Cigars
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <a href="/wiki/Cigar" title="Cigar">
        Cigars
       </a>
       are tightly rolled bundles of dried and fermented tobacco which are ignited so that smoke may be drawn into the smoker's mouth. They are generally not inhaled because of the high alkalinity of the smoke, which can quickly become irritating to the trachea and lungs. The prevalence of cigar smoking varies depending on location, historical period, and population surveyed, and prevalence estimates vary somewhat depending on the survey method. The United States is the top consuming country by far, followed by Germany and the United Kingdom; the US and Western Europe account for about 75% of cigar sales worldwide.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rarick_45-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Rarick-45">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         45
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 2005 it is estimated that 4.3% of men and 0.3% of women smoke cigars in the USA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         46
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Cigarettes
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cigarette" title="Cigarette">
         Cigarettes
        </a>
       </i>
       , French for "small cigar", are a product consumed through smoking and manufactured out of cured and finely cut tobacco leaves and reconstituted tobacco, often combined with other additives, which are then rolled or stuffed into a paper-wrapped cylinder.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHOJeffreyWigand_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-WHOJeffreyWigand-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cigarettes are ignited and inhaled, usually through a cellulose acetate filter, into the mouth and lungs. Although rarely practiced, cigarettes can also be consumed
       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoke_enema" title="Tobacco smoke enema">
        rectally
       </a>
       by inhaling the smoke into the mouth and pushing it through a pipe into the rectum.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         47
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <p>
      <span id="French_inhale">
      </span>
     </p>
     <dl>
      <dt>
       Hookah
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Hookah" title="Hookah">
         Hookah
        </a>
       </i>
       are a single or multi-stemmed (often glass-based) water pipe for smoking. Originally from India. The hookah was a symbol of pride and honour for the landlords, kings and other such high class people. Now, the hookah has gained immense popularity, especially in the Middle East. A hookah operates by water filtration and indirect heat. It can be used for smoking herbal fruits, tobacco, or
       <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">
        cannabis
       </a>
       .
      </dd>
      <dt>
       Kretek
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Kretek" title="Kretek">
         Kretek
        </a>
       </i>
       are cigarettes made with a complex blend of tobacco,
       <a href="/wiki/Clove" title="Clove">
        cloves
       </a>
       and a flavoring "sauce". It was first introduced in the 1880s in Kudus, Java, to deliver the medicinal eugenol of cloves to the lungs. The quality and variety of tobacco play an important role in kretek production, from which kretek can contain more than 30 types of tobacco. Minced dried clove buds weighing about 1/3 of the tobacco blend are added to add flavoring. In 2004 the United States prohibited cigarettes from having a "characterizing flavor" of certain ingredients other than tobacco and menthol, thereby removing kretek from being classified as cigarettes.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         48
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </dd>
      <dt>
       Passive smoking
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <a href="/wiki/Passive_smoking" title="Passive smoking">
        Passive smoking
       </a>
       is the usually involuntary consumption of smoked tobacco. Second-hand smoke (SHS) is the consumption where the burning end is present, environmental tobacco smoke (ETS) or
       <a href="/wiki/Third-hand_smoke" title="Third-hand smoke">
        third-hand smoke
       </a>
       is the consumption of the smoke that remains after the burning end has been extinguished. Because of its perceived negative implications, this form of consumption has played a central role in the regulation of tobacco products.
      </dd>
      <dt>
       Pipe smoking
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <a href="/wiki/Pipe_smoking" title="Pipe smoking">
        Pipe smoking
       </a>
       typically consists of a small chamber (the bowl) for the combustion of the tobacco to be smoked and a thin stem (shank) that ends in a mouthpiece (the bit). Shredded pieces of tobacco are placed into the chamber and ignited. Tobaccos for smoking in pipes are often carefully treated and blended to achieve flavour nuances not available in other tobacco products.
      </dd>
      <dt>
       Roll-Your-Own
      </dt>
      <dd>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roll-Your-Own" title="Roll-Your-Own">
        Roll-Your-Own
       </a>
       or hand-rolled cigarettes, often called "rollies", "cigi" or "Roll-ups", are very popular particularly in European countries and the UK. These are prepared from loose tobacco, cigarette papers, and filters all bought separately. They are usually much cheaper than ready-made cigarettes and small contraptions can be bought making the process easier.
      </dd>
      <dt>
       Vaporizer
      </dt>
      <dd>
       A
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vaporizer_(cannabis)" title="Vaporizer (cannabis)">
        vaporizer
       </a>
       is a device used to sublimate the active ingredients of plant material. Rather than burning the herb, which produces potentially irritating, toxic, or
       <a href="/wiki/Carcinogen" title="Carcinogen">
        carcinogenic
       </a>
       by-products; a vaporizer heats the material in a partial vacuum so that the active compounds contained in the plant boil off into a vapor. This method is often preferable when medically administrating the smoke substance, as opposed to directly pyrolyzing the plant material.
      </dd>
     </dl>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Physiology">
       Physiology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Physiology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Chain_smoking" title="Chain smoking">
       Chain smoking
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="513" data-file-width="650" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg/220px-Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg/330px-Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg/440px-Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blood_nicotine_graph.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A graph that shows the efficiency of smoking as a way to absorb nicotine compared to other forms of intake.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The active substances in tobacco, especially cigarettes, are administered by burning the leaves and inhaling the vaporised gas that results. This quickly and effectively delivers substances into the bloodstream by absorption through the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveoli" title="Alveoli">
       alveoli
      </a>
      in the lungs. The lungs contain some 300 million alveoli, which amounts to a surface area of over 70m
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      (about the size of a tennis court). This method is not completely efficient as not all of the smoke will be inhaled, and some amount of the active substances will be lost in the process of combustion,
      <a href="/wiki/Pyrolysis" title="Pyrolysis">
       pyrolysis
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GilmanXun2004p318_9-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-GilmanXun2004p318-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Pipe and Cigar smoke are not inhaled because of its high
      <a href="/wiki/Alkalinity" title="Alkalinity">
       alkalinity
      </a>
      , which are irritating to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertebrate_trachea" title="Vertebrate trachea">
       trachea
      </a>
      and lungs. However, because of its higher alkalinity (pH 8.5) compared to cigarette smoke (pH 5.3), non-ionised nicotine is more readily absorbed through the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mucous_membranes" title="Mucous membranes">
       mucous membranes
      </a>
      in the mouth.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
       <a href="#cite_note-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nicotine absorption from cigar and pipe, however, is much less than that from cigarette smoke.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nicotine and cocaine activate similar patterns of neurons, which supports the idea that common
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enzyme_substrate" title="Enzyme substrate">
       substrates
      </a>
      among these drugs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
       <a href="#cite_note-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The inhaled
      <a href="/wiki/Nicotine" title="Nicotine">
       nicotine
      </a>
      mimics
      <a href="/wiki/Nicotinic_acetylcholine_receptor" title="Nicotinic acetylcholine receptor">
       nicotinic acetylcholine
      </a>
      which when bound to
      <a href="/wiki/Nicotinic_acetylcholine_receptor" title="Nicotinic acetylcholine receptor">
       nicotinic acetylcholine receptors
      </a>
      prevents the reuptake of
      <a href="/wiki/Acetylcholine" title="Acetylcholine">
       acetylcholine
      </a>
      thereby increasing that
      <a href="/wiki/Neurotransmitter" title="Neurotransmitter">
       neurotransmitter
      </a>
      in those areas of the body.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WonnacottPMID9023878_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WonnacottPMID9023878-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These
      <a href="/wiki/Nicotinic_acetylcholine_receptor" title="Nicotinic acetylcholine receptor">
       nicotinic acetylcholine receptors
      </a>
      are located in the central nervous system and at the nerve-muscle junction of skeletal muscles; whose activity increases heart rate, alertness,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PMID2498936_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-PMID2498936-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and faster reaction times.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WesnessWarburton1997_11-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WesnessWarburton1997-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nicotine acetylcholine stimulation is not directly addictive. However, since dopamine-releasing neurons are abundant on nicotine receptors, dopamine is released; and, in the
      <a href="/wiki/Nucleus_accumbens" title="Nucleus accumbens">
       nucleus accumbens
      </a>
      , dopamine is associated with motivation causing
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reinforcing" title="Reinforcing">
       reinforcing
      </a>
      behavior.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Dopamine increase, in the
      <a href="/wiki/Prefrontal_Cortex_Basal_Ganglia_Working_Memory" title="Prefrontal Cortex Basal Ganglia Working Memory">
       prefrontal cortex
      </a>
      , may also increase
      <a href="/wiki/Working_memory" title="Working memory">
       working memory
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      When tobacco is smoked, most of the nicotine is pyrolyzed. However, a dose sufficient to cause mild somatic dependency and mild to strong psychological dependency remains. There is also a formation of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harmala" title="Harmala">
       harmane
      </a>
      (a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MAO_inhibitor" title="MAO inhibitor">
       MAO inhibitor
      </a>
      ) from the acetaldehyde in tobacco smoke. This may play a role in nicotine addiction, by facilitating a dopamine release in the
      <a href="/wiki/Nucleus_accumbens" title="Nucleus accumbens">
       nucleus accumbens
      </a>
      as a response to nicotine stimuli.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Using rat studies, withdrawal after repeated exposure to nicotine results in less responsive nucleus accumbens cells, which produce dopamine responsible for
      <a href="/wiki/Reinforcement" title="Reinforcement">
       reinforcement
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
       Demographics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Demographics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Prevalence_of_tobacco_consumption" title="Prevalence of tobacco consumption">
       Prevalence of tobacco consumption
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px">
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Female_Smoking_by_Country.png">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="1800" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Female_Smoking_by_Country.png/200px-Female_Smoking_by_Country.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Female_Smoking_by_Country.png/300px-Female_Smoking_by_Country.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Female_Smoking_by_Country.png/400px-Female_Smoking_by_Country.png 2x" width="200"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Percentage of
         <b>
          females
         </b>
         smoking any tobacco product
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
        <div class="thumbimage">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Male_Smoking_by_Country.png">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="820" data-file-width="1800" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Male_Smoking_by_Country.png/200px-Male_Smoking_by_Country.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Male_Smoking_by_Country.png/300px-Male_Smoking_by_Country.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Male_Smoking_by_Country.png/400px-Male_Smoking_by_Country.png 2x" width="200"/>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
         Percentage of
         <b>
          males
         </b>
         smoking any tobacco product. Note that there is a difference between the scales used for females and the scales used for males.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MPOWER_2008_pp.3D267.E2.80.93288_42-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-MPOWER_2008_pp.3D267.E2.80.93288-42">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           42
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      As of 2000, smoking was practised by around 1.22 billion people. At current rates of 'smoker replacement' and market growth, this may reach around 1.9 billion in 2025.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HNPGuindonBoisclair13-16_57-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-HNPGuindonBoisclair13-16-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Smoking may be up to five times more prevalent amongst men than women in some communities,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HNPGuindonBoisclair13-16_57-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-HNPGuindonBoisclair13-16-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      although the gender gap usually declines with younger age.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WomenTobaccoChallenges5-6_14-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WomenTobaccoChallenges5-6-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001SurgeonGeneralWomen47_15-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-2001SurgeonGeneralWomen47-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In some developed countries smoking rates for men have peaked and begun to decline, while for women they continue to climb.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      As of 2002, about twenty percent of young teenagers (1315) smoked worldwide. From which 80,000 to 100,000 children begin smoking every day, roughly half of whom live in Asia. Half of those who begin smoking in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adolescent" title="Adolescent">
       adolescent
      </a>
      years are projected to go on to smoke for 15 to 20 years.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2002FactSheet_7-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2002FactSheet-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">
       World Health Organization
      </a>
      (WHO) states that "Much of the disease burden and premature mortality attributable to tobacco use disproportionately affect the poor". Of the 1.22 billion smokers, 1 billion of them live in developing or transitional economies. Rates of smoking have leveled off or declined in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_world" title="Developed world">
       developed world
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_world" title="Developing world">
       developing world
      </a>
      , however, tobacco consumption is rising by 3.4% per year as of 2002.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2002FactSheet_7-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2002FactSheet-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The WHO in 2004 projected 58.8 million deaths to occur globally,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2004GBD8_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2004GBD8-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      from which 5.4 million are tobacco-attributed,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 4.9 million as of 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2007FactSheet_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2007FactSheet-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As of 2002, 70% of the deaths are in developing countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2007FactSheet_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2007FactSheet-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Psychology">
       Psychology
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Psychology">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Takeup">
       Takeup
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Takeup">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1066" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg/170px-Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg/255px-Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg/340px-Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sigmund_Freud_LIFE.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud" title="Sigmund Freud">
         Sigmund Freud
        </a>
        , whose doctor
        <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud#Death" title="Sigmund Freud">
         assisted his suicide
        </a>
        because of
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_cancer" title="Oral cancer">
         oral cancer
        </a>
        caused by smoking
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gay_63-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Gay-63">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          63
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Most smokers begin during adolescence or early adulthood.Some studies also show that smoking can also be linked to various mental health complications.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smoking has elements of risk-taking and rebellion, which often appeal to young people. The presence of peers that smoke and media featuring high-status models smoking may also encourage smoking. Because teenagers are influenced more by their peers than by adults, attempts by parents, schools, and health professionals at preventing people from trying cigarettes are often unsuccessful.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-StantonSilva1992_65-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-StantonSilva1992-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Children of smoking parents are more likely to smoke than children with non-smoking parents. One study found that parental smoking cessation was associated with less adolescent smoking, except when the other parent currently smoked.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A current study tested the relation of adolescent smoking to rules regulating where adults are allowed to smoke in the home. Results showed that restrictive home smoking policies were associated with lower likelihood of trying smoking for both middle and high school students.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
       <a href="#cite_note-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Behavioural research generally indicates that teenagers begin their smoking habits due to peer pressure, and cultural influence portrayed by friends. However, one study found that direct pressure to smoke cigarettes played a less significant part in adolescent smoking, with
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adolescent" title="Adolescent">
       adolescents
      </a>
      also reporting low levels of both
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norm_(sociology)" title="Norm (sociology)">
       normative
      </a>
      and direct pressure to smoke cigarettes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
       <a href="#cite_note-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A similar study suggested that individuals may play a more active role in starting to smoke than has previously been thought and that social processes other than peer pressure also need to be taken into account.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Another study's results indicated that
      <a href="/wiki/Peer_pressure" title="Peer pressure">
       peer pressure
      </a>
      was significantly associated with smoking behaviour across all age and gender cohorts, but that intrapersonal factors were significantly more important to the smoking behaviour of 12- to 13-year-old girls than same-age boys. Within the 14- to 15-year-old age group, one peer pressure variable emerged as a significantly more important predictor of girls' than boys' smoking.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is debated whether peer pressure or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-selection" title="Self-selection">
       self-selection
      </a>
      is a greater cause of adolescent smoking.
     </p>
     <p>
      Psychologists such as
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Eysenck" title="Hans Eysenck">
       Hans Eysenck
      </a>
      have developed a personality profile for the typical smoker.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extraversion" title="Extraversion">
       Extraversion
      </a>
      is the trait that is most associated with smoking, and smokers tend to be sociable, impulsive, risk taking, and excitement seeking individuals.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although personality and social factors may make people likely to smoke, the actual habit is a function of
      <a href="/wiki/Operant_conditioning" title="Operant conditioning">
       operant conditioning
      </a>
      . During the early stages, smoking provides pleasurable sensations (because of its action on the
      <a href="/wiki/Dopamine" title="Dopamine">
       dopamine
      </a>
      system) and thus serves as a source of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positive_reinforcement" title="Positive reinforcement">
       positive reinforcement
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Persistence">
       Persistence
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Persistence">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The reasons given by some smokers for this activity have been categorised as
      <i>
       addictive smoking
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       pleasure from smoking
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       tension reduction/relaxation
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       social smoking
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       stimulation
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       habit/automatism
      </i>
      , and
      <i>
       handling
      </i>
      . There are gender differences in how much each of these reasons contribute, with females more likely than males to cite
      <i>
       tension reduction/relaxation
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       stimulation
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       social smoking
      </i>
      .
