      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some smokers argue that the
      <a href="/wiki/Depressant" title="Depressant">
       depressant
      </a>
      effect of smoking allows them to calm their nerves, often allowing for increased concentration. However, according to the
      <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">
       Imperial College London
      </a>
      , "Nicotine seems to provide both a stimulant and a depressant effect, and it is likely that the effect it has at any time is determined by the mood of the user, the environment and the circumstances of use. Studies have suggested that low doses have a depressant effect, while higher doses have stimulant effect."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Patterns">
       Patterns
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Patterns">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      A number of studies have established that cigarette sales and smoking follow distinct time-related patterns. For example, cigarette sales in the United States of America have been shown to follow a strongly seasonal pattern, with the high months being the months of summer, and the low months being the winter months.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Similarly, smoking has been shown to follow distinct circadian patterns during the waking daywith the high point usually occurring shortly after waking in the morning, and shortly before going to sleep at night.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">
       Impact
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Impact">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economic">
       Economic
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economic">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_industry" title="Tobacco industry">
       Tobacco industry
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In countries where there is a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universal_healthcare" title="Universal healthcare">
       universally funded healthcare
      </a>
      system, the government covers the cost of medical care for smokers who become ill through smoking in the form of increased taxes. Two broad debating positions exist on this front, the "pro-smoking" argument suggesting that heavy smokers generally don't live long enough to develop the costly and chronic illnesses which affect the elderly, reducing society's healthcare burden, and the "anti-smoking" argument suggests that the healthcare burden is increased because smokers get chronic illnesses younger and at a higher rate than the general population. Data on both positions has been contested. The
      <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">
       Centers for Disease Control and Prevention
      </a>
      published research in 2002 claiming that the cost of each
      <a href="/wiki/Cigarette_pack" title="Cigarette pack">
       pack
      </a>
      of cigarettes sold in the United States was more than $7 in medical care and lost productivity.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-query.nytimes.com_77-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-query.nytimes.com-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The cost may be higher, with another study putting it as high as $41 per pack, most of which however is on the individual and his/her family.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Familycost_78-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Familycost-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This is how one author of that study puts it when he explains the very low cost for others: "The reason the number is low is that for private pensions, Social Security, and Medicare  the biggest factors in calculating costs to society  smoking actually saves money. Smokers die at a younger age and don't draw on the funds they've paid into those systems."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Familycost_78-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Familycost-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Other research demonstrates that premature death caused by smoking may redistribute Social Security income in unexpected ways that affect behavior and reduce the economic well-being of smokers and their dependents.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To further support this, whatever the rate of smoking consumption is per day, smokers have a greater lifetime medical cost on average compared to a non smoker by an estimated $6000
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barendregt.2C_J._J._1997_80-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Barendregt.2C_J._J._1997-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Between the cost for lost productivity and health care expenditures combined, cigarette smoking costs at least 193 billion dollars. (Research also shows that smokers earn less money than nonsmokers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ) As for secondhand smoke, the cost is over 10 billion dollars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      By contrast, some non-scientific studies, including one conducted by
      <a href="/wiki/Philip_Morris_International" title="Philip Morris International">
       Philip Morris
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
       Czech Republic
      </a>
      called
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Public_Finance_Balance_of_Smoking_in_the_Czech_Republic" title="Public Finance Balance of Smoking in the Czech Republic">
        Public Finance Balance of Smoking in the Czech Republic
       </a>
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Czechonomics_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Czechonomics-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and another by the
      <a href="/wiki/Cato_Institute" title="Cato Institute">
       Cato Institute
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      support the opposite position. Philip Morris has explicitly apologised for the former study, saying: "The funding and public release of this study which, among other things, detailed purported cost savings to the Czech Republic due to premature deaths of smokers, exhibited terrible judgment as well as a complete and unacceptable disregard of basic human values. For one of our tobacco companies to commission this study was not just a terrible mistake, it was wrong. All of us at Philip Morris, no matter where we work, are extremely sorry for this. No one benefits from the very real, serious and significant diseases caused by smoking."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Czechonomics_83-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Czechonomics-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Between 1970 and 1995, per-capita cigarette consumption in poorer developing countries increased by 67 percent, while it dropped by 10 percent in the richer developed world. Eighty percent of smokers now live in less developed countries. By 2030, the
      <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">
       World Health Organization
      </a>
      (WHO) forecasts that 10 million people a year will die of smoking-related illness, making it the single biggest cause of death worldwide, with the largest increase to be among women. WHO forecasts the 21st century's death rate from smoking to be ten times the 20th century's rate. ("Washingtonian" magazine, December 2007)
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">
       Health
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Health">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Health_effects_of_tobacco" title="Health effects of tobacco">
       Health effects of tobacco
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Cigarette smoking is the leading cause of preventable death and a major public health concern.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg">
        <img alt="head and torso of a male with internal organs shown and labels referring to the effects of tobacco smoking" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1240" data-file-width="1180" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg/220px-Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg/330px-Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg/440px-Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Adverse_effects_of_tobacco_smoking.svg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Common adverse effects of tobacco smoking. The more common effects are in bold face.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
         <a href="#cite_note-86">
          <span>
           [
          </span>
          86
          <span>
           ]
          </span>
         </a>
        </sup>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Tobacco use leads most commonly to diseases affecting the heart and lungs, with smoking being a major risk factor for
      <a href="/wiki/Myocardial_infarction" title="Myocardial infarction">
       heart attacks
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Stroke" title="Stroke">
       strokes
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease" title="Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease">
       chronic obstructive pulmonary disease
      </a>
      (COPD),
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emphysema" title="Emphysema">
       emphysema
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">
       cancer
      </a>
      (particularly
      <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">
       lung cancer
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Laryngeal_cancer" title="Laryngeal cancer">
       cancers of the larynx
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Oral_cancer" title="Oral cancer">
       mouth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Esophageal_cancer" title="Esophageal cancer">
       esophageal cancer
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Pancreatic_cancer" title="Pancreatic cancer">
       pancreatic cancer
      </a>
      ). Cigarette smoking increases the risk of Crohn's disease as well as the severity of the course of the disease.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is also the number one cause of
      <a href="/wiki/Bladder_cancer" title="Bladder cancer">
       bladder cancer
      </a>
      . The smoke from tobacco elicits carcinogenic effects on the tissues of the body that are exposed to the smoke.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Tobacco smoke can combine with other carcinogens present within the environment in order to produce elevated degrees of lung cancer.
     </p>
     <p>
      Cigarette smoking has also been associated with sarcopenia, the age-related loss of muscle mass and strength.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">
       World Health Organization
      </a>
      estimates that tobacco caused 5.4 million deaths in 2004
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO_90-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 100 million deaths over the course of the 20th century.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2_91-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WHO2-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Similarly, the United States
      <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">
       Centers for Disease Control and Prevention
      </a>
      describes tobacco use as "the single most important preventable risk to human health in developed countries and an important cause of premature death worldwide."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fn1_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-fn1-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although 70% of smokers state their intention to quit only 3-5% are actually successful in doing so.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barendregt.2C_J._J._1997_80-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Barendregt.2C_J._J._1997-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The probabilities of death from
      <a href="/wiki/Lung_cancer" title="Lung cancer">
       Lung cancer
      </a>
      before age 75 in the United Kingdom are 0.2% for men who never smoked (0.4% for women), 5.5% for male former smokers (2.6% in women), 15.9% for current male smokers (9.5% for women) and 24.4% for male heavy smokers defined as smoking more than 5 cigarettes per day (18.5% for women).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Tobacco smoke can combine with other carcinogens present within the environment in order to produce elevated degrees of lung cancer.
     </p>
     <p>
      Rates of smoking have generally levelled-off or declined in the developed world. Smoking rates in the United States have dropped by half from 1965 to 2006 falling from 42% to 20.8% in adults.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
       <a href="#cite_note-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the developing world, tobacco consumption is rising by 3.4% per year.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
       <a href="#cite_note-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second-hand_smoke" title="Second-hand smoke">
       Second-hand smoke
      </a>
      presents a very real health risk, to which six hundred thousand deaths were attributed in 2004. It also has been known to produce skin conditions such as freckles and dryness.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lancet-2nd-burden_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lancet-2nd-burden-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2015, a meta-analysis found that smokers were at greater risk of developing psychotic illness.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
       <a href="#cite_note-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Social">
       Social
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Social">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_advertising" title="Tobacco advertising">
       Tobacco advertising
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Religious_views_on_smoking" title="Religious views on smoking">
       Religious views on smoking
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Famous smokers of the past used cigarettes or pipes as part of their image, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre" title="Jean-Paul Sartre">
       Jean-Paul Sartre
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Gauloises" title="Gauloises">
       Gauloises
      </a>
      -brand cigarettes;
      <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">
       Albert Einstein
      </a>
      's,
      <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">
       Douglas MacArthur
      </a>
      's,
      <a href="/wiki/Bertrand_Russell" title="Bertrand Russell">
       Bertrand Russell
      </a>
      's, and Bing Crosby's pipes; or the news broadcaster
      <a href="/wiki/Edward_R._Murrow" title="Edward R. Murrow">
       Edward R. Murrow
      </a>
      's cigarette. Writers in particular seem to be known for smoking, for example, Cornell Professor Richard Klein's book
      <i>
       Cigarettes are Sublime
      </i>
      for the analysis, by this professor of French literature, of the role smoking plays in 19th and 20th century letters. The popular author
      <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Vonnegut" title="Kurt Vonnegut">
       Kurt Vonnegut
      </a>
      addressed his addiction to cigarettes within his novels. British Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Harold_Wilson" title="Harold Wilson">
       Harold Wilson
      </a>
      was well known for smoking a pipe in public as was
      <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">
       Winston Churchill
      </a>
      for his cigars.
      <a href="/wiki/Sherlock_Holmes" title="Sherlock Holmes">
       Sherlock Holmes
      </a>
      , the fictional detective created by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_Conan_Doyle" title="Sir Arthur Conan Doyle">
       Sir Arthur Conan Doyle
      </a>
      smoked a pipe, cigarettes, and cigars. The
      <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">
       DC
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vertigo_Comics" title="Vertigo Comics">
       Vertigo
      </a>
      comic book character,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Constantine" title="John Constantine">
       John Constantine
      </a>
      , created by
      <a href="/wiki/Alan_Moore" title="Alan Moore">
       Alan Moore
      </a>
      , is synonymous with smoking, so much so that the first storyline by
      <a href="/wiki/Preacher_(comics)" title="Preacher (comics)">
       Preacher
      </a>
      creator,
      <a href="/wiki/Garth_Ennis" title="Garth Ennis">
       Garth Ennis
      </a>
      , centered around John Constantine contracting lung cancer.
      <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">
       Professional wrestler
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/The_Sandman_(wrestler)" title="The Sandman (wrestler)">
       James Fullington
      </a>
      , while in character as "The Sandman", is a chronic smoker in order to appear "tough".
     </p>
     <p>
      The problem of smoking at home is particularly difficult for women in many cultures (especially Arab cultures), where it may not be acceptable for a woman to ask her husband not to smoke at home or in the presence of her children. Studies have shown that pollution levels for smoking areas indoors are higher than levels found on busy roadways, in closed motor garages, and during fire storms.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (October 2012)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Furthermore, smoke can spread from one room to another, even if doors to the smoking area are closed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
       <a href="#cite_note-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The ceremonial smoking of tobacco, and praying with a
      <a href="/wiki/Calumet_(pipe)" title="Calumet (pipe)">
       sacred pipe
      </a>
      , is a prominent part of the religious ceremonies of a number of
      <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">
       Native American
      </a>
      Nations.
      <i>
       Sema
      </i>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Anishinaabe" title="Anishinaabe">
       Anishinaabe
      </a>
      word for tobacco, is grown for ceremonial use and considered the ultimate sacred plant since its smoke was believed to carry prayers to the heavens. In most major religions, however, tobacco smoking is not specifically prohibited, although it may be discouraged as an immoral habit. Before the health risks of smoking were identified through controlled study, smoking was considered an immoral habit by certain Christian preachers and social reformers. The founder of the
      <a href="/wiki/Latter_Day_Saint_movement" title="Latter Day Saint movement">
       Latter Day Saint movement
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Smith" title="Joseph Smith">
       Joseph Smith
      </a>
      , recorded that on February 27, 1833, he received a
      <a href="/wiki/Revelation" title="Revelation">
       revelation
      </a>
      which discouraged tobacco use. This "Word of Wisdom" was later accepted as a commandment, and faithful Latter-day Saints abstain completely from tobacco.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Jehovah's Witnesses base their stand against smoking on the Bible's command to "clean ourselves of every defilement of flesh" (2 Corinthians 7:1). The Jewish Rabbi
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yisrael_Meir_Kagan" title="Yisrael Meir Kagan">
       Yisrael Meir Kagan
      </a>
      (18381933) was one of the first Jewish authorities to speak out on smoking. In
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ahmadiyya_Islam" title="Ahmadiyya Islam">
       Ahmadiyya Islam
      </a>
      , smoking is highly discouraged, although not forbidden. During the month of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ramadhan" title="Ramadhan">
       fasting
      </a>
      however, it is forbidden to smoke tobacco.,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the
      <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah' Faith">
       Bah' Faith
      </a>
      , smoking tobacco is too discouraged though not forbidden.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneworld_101-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-oneworld-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_policy">
       Public policy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Public policy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_politics" title="Tobacco politics">
       Tobacco politics
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      On February 27, 2005 the
      <a href="/wiki/WHO_Framework_Convention_on_Tobacco_Control" title="WHO Framework Convention on Tobacco Control">
       WHO Framework Convention on Tobacco Control
      </a>
      , took effect. The FCTC is the world's first public health treaty. Countries that sign on as parties agree to a set of common goals, minimum standards for tobacco control policy, and to cooperate in dealing with cross-border challenges such as cigarette smuggling. Currently the WHO declares that 4 billion people will be covered by the treaty, which includes 168 signatories.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Among other steps, signatories are to put together legislation that will eliminate secondhand smoke in indoor workplaces, public transport, indoor public places and, as appropriate, other public places.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">
       Taxation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Taxation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Cigarette_taxes_in_the_United_States" title="Cigarette taxes in the United States">
       Cigarette taxes in the United States
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Many governments have introduced
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Excise_tax" title="Excise tax">
       excise taxes
      </a>
      on cigarettes in order to reduce the consumption of cigarettes.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2002, the
      <a href="/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention" title="Centers for Disease Control and Prevention">
       Centers for Disease Control and Prevention
      </a>
      said that each
      <a href="/wiki/Cigarette_pack" title="Cigarette pack">
       pack
      </a>
      of cigarettes sold in the United States costs the nation more than $7 in medical care and lost productivity,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-query.nytimes.com_77-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-query.nytimes.com-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      around $3400 per year per smoker. Another study by a team of health economists finds the combined price paid by their families and society is about $41 per pack of cigarettes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Substantial scientific evidence shows that higher cigarette prices result in lower overall cigarette consumption. Most studies indicate that a 10% increase in price will reduce overall cigarette consumption by 3% to 5%. Youth, minorities, and low-income smokers are two to three times more likely to quit or smoke less than other smokers in response to price increases.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
       <a href="#cite_note-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Smoking is often cited
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      as an example of an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inelastic_good" title="Inelastic good">
       inelastic good
      </a>
      , however, i.e. a large rise in price will only result in a small decrease in consumption.
     </p>
     <p>
      Many nations have implemented some form of tobacco taxation. As of 1997, Denmark had the highest cigarette tax burden of $4.02 per pack. Taiwan only had a tax burden of $0.62 per pack. The federal government of the United States charges $1.01 per pack.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
       <a href="#cite_note-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Cigarette taxes vary widely from state to state in the United States. For example,
      <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">
       Missouri
      </a>
      has a cigarette tax of only 17 cents per pack, the nation's lowest, while
      <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">
       New York
      </a>
      has the highest cigarette tax in the U.S.: $4.35 per pack. In Alabama, Illinois, Missouri, New York City, Tennessee, and Virginia, counties and cities may impose an additional limited tax on the price of cigarettes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Sales taxes are also levied on tobacco products in most jurisdictions.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the United Kingdom, a packet of 20 cigarettes typically costs between and at 2007 prices, depending on the brand purchased and where the purchase was made.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
       <a href="#cite_note-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The UK has a significant
      <a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">
       black market
      </a>
      for tobacco, and it has been estimated by the tobacco industry that 27% of cigarette and 68% of handrolling tobacco consumption is non-UK duty paid (NUKDP).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In Australia total taxes account for 62.5% of the final price of a packet of cigarettes (2011 figures). These taxes include federal excise or customs duty, and
      <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_Services_Tax_(Australia)" title="Goods and Services Tax (Australia)">
       Goods and Services Tax (Australia)
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Restrictions">
       Restrictions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Restrictions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Smoking_area.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2173" data-file-width="1537" height="311" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Smoking_area.JPG/220px-Smoking_area.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Smoking_area.JPG/330px-Smoking_area.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Smoking_area.JPG/440px-Smoking_area.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Smoking_area.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        An enclosed smoking area in a Japanese train station. Notice the air vent on the roof.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_advertising" title="Tobacco advertising">
       Tobacco advertising
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_packaging_warning_messages" title="Tobacco packaging warning messages">
       Tobacco packaging warning messages
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Smoking_ban" title="Smoking ban">
       Smoking ban
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In June 1967, the US
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">
       Federal Communications Commission
      </a>
      ruled that programmes broadcast on a television station which discussed smoking and health were insufficient to offset the effects of paid advertisements that were broadcast for five to ten minutes each day. In April 1970, the US Congress passed the
      <a href="/wiki/Public_Health_Cigarette_Smoking_Act" title="Public Health Cigarette Smoking Act">
       Public Health Cigarette Smoking Act
      </a>
      banning the advertising of cigarettes on
      <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">
       television
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">
       radio
      </a>
      starting on January 2, 1971.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Tobacco Advertising Prohibition Act 1992 expressly prohibited almost all forms of Tobacco advertising in Australia, including the sponsorship of sporting or other cultural events by cigarette brands.
     </p>
     <p>
      All tobacco advertising and sponsorship on television has been banned within the European Union since 1991 under the Television Without Frontiers Directive (1989).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This ban was extended by the Tobacco Advertising Directive, which took effect in July 2005 to cover other forms of media such as the internet, print media, and radio. The directive does not include advertising in cinemas and on billboards or using merchandising  or tobacco sponsorship of cultural and sporting events which are purely local, with participants coming from only one Member State
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
       <a href="#cite_note-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      as these fall outside the jurisdiction of the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">
       European Commission
      </a>
      . However, most member states have transposed the directive with national laws that are wider in scope than the directive and cover local advertising. A 2008 European Commission report concluded that the directive had been successfully transposed into national law in all EU member states, and that these laws were well implemented.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
       <a href="#cite_note-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Some countries also impose legal requirements on the packaging of tobacco products. For example in the countries of the European Union, Turkey, Australia
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auswarn_115-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-auswarn-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and South Africa, cigarette packs must be prominently labeled with the health risks associated with smoking.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Canada, Australia, Thailand, Iceland and Brazil have also imposed labels upon cigarette packs warning smokers of the effects, and they include graphic images of the potential health effects of smoking. Cards are also inserted into cigarette packs in Canada. There are sixteen of them, and only one comes in a pack. They explain different methods of quitting smoking. Also, in the United Kingdom, there have been a number of graphic
      <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">
       NHS
      </a>
      advertisements, one showing a cigarette filled with fatty deposits, as if the cigarette is symbolising the artery of a smoker.
     </p>
     <p>
      Many countries have a
      <a href="/wiki/Smoking_age" title="Smoking age">
       smoking age
      </a>
      . In many countries, including the United States, most European Union member states, New Zealand, Canada, South Africa, Israel, India, Brazil, Chile, Costa Rica and Australia, it is illegal to sell tobacco products to minors and in the Netherlands, Austria, Belgium, Denmark and South Africa it is illegal to sell tobacco products to people under the age of 16. On September 1, 2007 the minimum age to buy tobacco products in Germany rose from 16 to 18, as well as in the United Kingdom where on October 1, 2007 it rose from 16 to 18.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Underlying such laws is the belief that people should make an informed decision regarding the risks of tobacco use. These laws have a lax enforcement in some nations and states. In China, Turkey, and many other countries usually a child will have little problem buying tobacco products, because they are often told to go to the store to buy tobacco for their parents.
     </p>
     <p>
      Several countries such as
      <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">
       Ireland
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">
       Latvia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">
       Estonia
      </a>
      , the Netherlands, Finland, Norway, Canada, Australia, Sweden, Portugal,
      <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
       Singapore
      </a>
      , Italy,
      <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
       Indonesia
      </a>
      , India,
      <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">
       Lithuania
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
       Chile
      </a>
      , Spain,
      <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">
       Iceland
      </a>
      , United Kingdom,
      <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">
       Slovenia
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
       Turkey
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">
       Malta
      </a>
      have legislated against smoking in public places, often including bars and restaurants. Restaurateurs have been permitted in some jurisdictions to build designated smoking areas (or to prohibit smoking). In the United States, many states prohibit smoking in restaurants, and some also prohibit smoking in bars. In provinces of Canada, smoking is illegal in indoor workplaces and public places, including bars and restaurants. As of March 31, 2008 Canada has introduced a smoke-free law ban in all public places, as well as within 10 metres of an entrance to any public place. In Australia, smoke-free laws vary from state to state. Currently, Queensland has completely smoke-free indoor public places (including workplaces, bars, pubs and eateries) as well as patrolled beaches and some outdoor public areas. There are, however, exceptions for designated smoking areas. In
      <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">
       Victoria
      </a>
      , smoking is restricted in railway stations, bus stops and tram stops as these are public locations where
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second-hand_smoke" title="Second-hand smoke">
       second-hand smoke
      </a>
      can affect non-smokers waiting for public transport, and since July 1, 2007 is now extended to all indoor public places. In New Zealand and
      <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
       Brazil
      </a>
      , smoking is restricted in enclosed public places including bars, restaurants and pubs. Hong Kong restricted smoking on January 1, 2007 in the workplace, public spaces such as restaurants, karaoke rooms, buildings, and public parks (bars which do not admit minors were exempt until 2009). In
      <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
       Romania
      </a>
      smoking is illegal in trains, metro stations, public institutions (except where designated, usually outside) and public transport. In
      <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
       Germany
      </a>
      , additionally to smoking bans in public buildings and transports, an anti-smoking ordinance for bars and restaurants was implemented in late 2007. A study by the University of Hamburg (Ahlfeldt and Maennig 2010) demonstrates, that the smoking ban had, if any, only short run impacts on bar and restaurant revenues. In the medium and long run no negative effect was measurable. The results suggest either, that the consumption in bars and restaurants is not affected by smoking bans in the long run, or, that negative revenue impacts by smokers are compensated by increasing revenues through non-smokers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Ignition_safety">
       Ignition safety
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ignition safety">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      An indirect public health problem posed by cigarettes is that of accidental fires, usually linked with consumption of alcohol. Enhanced combustion using nitrates was traditionally used but cigarette manufacturors have been silent on this subject claiming at first that a safe cigarette was technically impossible, then that it could only be achieved by modifying the paper. Roll your own cigarettes contain no additives and are fire safe. Numerous
      <a href="/wiki/Fire_safe_cigarette" title="Fire safe cigarette">
       fire safe cigarette
      </a>
      designs have been proposed, some by tobacco companies themselves, which would extinguish a cigarette left unattended for more than a minute or two, thereby reducing the risk of fire. Among American tobacco companies, some have resisted this idea, while others have embraced it.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RJ_Reynolds" title="RJ Reynolds">
       RJ Reynolds
      </a>
      was a leader in making prototypes of these cigarettes in 1983
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
       <a href="#cite_note-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and will make all of their U.S. market cigarettes to be fire-safe by 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Philip_Morris_USA" title="Philip Morris USA">
       Phillip Morris
      </a>
      is not in active support of it.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letter_fire_safe_cigarettes_121-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-letter_fire_safe_cigarettes-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lorillard" title="Lorillard">
       Lorillard
      </a>
      , the US's third largest tobacco company, seems to be ambivalent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letter_fire_safe_cigarettes_121-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-letter_fire_safe_cigarettes-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Gateway_drug_theory">
       Gateway drug theory
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Gateway drug theory">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_and_other_drugs" title="Tobacco and other drugs">
       Tobacco and other drugs
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Gateway_drug_theory" title="Gateway drug theory">
       Gateway drug theory
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The relationship between tobacco and other drug use has been well-established, however the nature of this association remains unclear. The two main theories are the
      <a href="/wiki/Gateway_drug_theory" title="Gateway drug theory">
       phenotypic causation
      </a>
      (gateway) model and the correlated liabilities model. The causation model argues that smoking is a primary influence on future drug use,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while the correlated liabilities model argues that smoking and other drug use are predicated on genetic or environmental factors.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
       <a href="#cite_note-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cessation">
       Cessation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tobacco_smoking&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cessation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Smoking_cessation" title="Smoking cessation">
       Smoking cessation
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Smoking cessation, referred to as "quitting", is the action leading towards abstinence of tobacco smoking. Methods of "quitting" include
      <a href="/wiki/Cold_turkey" title="Cold turkey">
       cold turkey
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Nicotine_replacement_therapy" title="Nicotine replacement therapy">
       nicotine replacement therapy
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Antidepressant" title="Antidepressant">
       antidepressants
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hypnosis" title="Hypnosis">
       hypnosis
      </a>
      , self-help, and support groups.
     </p>
